    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           5,29
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,15
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 8.2 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          5.29 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.15 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    12,81
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        12,59
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 36.1 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 83.2% of the total average of 43.4   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 12.8 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 12.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,77
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,12
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 9.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.77 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.12 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,11
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     9,63
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         8,74
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 36.9 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 82.7% of the total average of 44.6   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 9.6 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          8.7 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,97
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,15
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 7.9 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.97 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.15 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,13
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    12,02
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        11,87
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 32.8 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 84.0% of the total average of 39.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 12.0 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 11.9 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,70
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,11
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 10.0 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.70 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.11 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,10
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     9,24
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         8,39
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 39.8 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 84.7% of the total average of 47.0   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 9.2 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          8.4 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,90
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,17
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 7.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.90 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.17 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,14
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    10,20
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        10,12
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 29.5 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 82.4% of the total average of 35.8   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 10.2 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 10.1 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,65
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,11
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 9.6 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.65 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.11 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,10
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     7,95
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         7,22
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 37.1 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 82.8% of the total average of 44.8   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 7.9 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          7.2 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,94
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,18
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 6.9 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.94 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.18 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     9,10
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         9,05
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 27.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 80.4% of the total average of 34.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 9.1 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          9.0 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,59
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,12
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 9.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.59 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.12 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,11
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     7,20
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         6,55
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 35.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 83.2% of the total average of 42.6   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 7.2 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          6.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           5,02
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,19
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 6.6 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          5.02 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.19 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,15
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     8,53
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         8,49
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 26.7 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 80.2% of the total average of 33.2   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 8.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          8.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           4,59
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,12
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 9.2 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to     
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          4.59 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.12 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,11
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                     6,95
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                         6,32
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 35.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 84.1% of the total average of 42.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 6.9 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced to  
          6.3 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.          
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().
